<p><b>Botswana</b> <span class="nowrap"><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'b' in 'buy'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">b</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ɒ/ short 'o' in 'body'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ɒ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'t' in 'tie'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">t</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ˈ</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">s</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'w' in 'wind'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">w</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ɑː/ 'a' in 'spa'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ɑː</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="'n' in 'nigh'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">n</span></a></span><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English#Key" title="Help:IPA for English"><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'" style="border-bottom:1px dotted">ə</span></a></span><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/</a></span></span>, officially the <b>Republic of Botswana</b> (<a href="/wiki/Tswana_language" title="Tswana language">Tswana</a>: <span lang="tn"><i>Lefatshe la Botswana</i></span>), is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> located in Southern Africa. The citizens refer to themselves as <i>Batswana</i> (singular: <i>Motswana</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Formerly the British <a href="/wiki/Protectorate" title="Protectorate">protectorate</a> of <a href="/wiki/Bechuanaland_Protectorate" title="Bechuanaland Protectorate">Bechuanaland</a>, Botswana adopted its new name after becoming independent within the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> on 30 September 1966.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Since then, it has maintained a strong tradition as a stable <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>, with a consistent record of uninterrupted democratic <a href="/wiki/Elections_in_Botswana" title="Elections in Botswana">elections</a>.</p>
<p>Geographically, Botswana is flat, with up to 70 percent of its territory being the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> to the south and southeast, <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a> to the west and north, and <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> to the northeast. Its border with <a href="/wiki/Zambia" title="Zambia">Zambia</a> to the north near <a href="/wiki/Kazungula,_Zambia" title="Kazungula, Zambia">Kazungula</a> is poorly defined but at most is a few hundred metres long.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A mid-sized country of just over two million people, Botswana is one of the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_population_density" title="List of countries by population density" class="mw-redirect">most sparsely populated</a> nations in the world. Around 10 percent of the population lives in the capital and largest city, <a href="/wiki/Gaborone" title="Gaborone">Gaborone</a>. Once one of the poorest countries in the world—with a GDP per capita of about US$70 per year in the late 1960s—Botswana has since transformed itself into one of the fastest-growing economies in the world, now boasting a GDP (<a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a>) per capita of about $16,400 per year as of 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> Its high <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">gross national income</a> (by some estimates the fourth-largest in Africa) gives the country a modest standard of living and the highest <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> of continental <a href="/wiki/Sub-Saharan_Africa" title="Sub-Saharan Africa">Sub-Saharan Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Botswana is a member of the <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Southern_African_Development_Community" title="Southern African Development Community">Southern African Development Community</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>. Despite its political stability and relative socioeconomic prosperity, the country is among the hardest hit by the <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Botswana" title="HIV/AIDS in Botswana">HIV/AIDS epidemic</a>, with around a quarter of the population estimated to be infected.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Botswana" title="History of Botswana">History of Botswana</a></div>
<p>In the 19th century, hostilities broke out between <a href="/wiki/Tswana_people" title="Tswana people">Tswana</a> inhabitants of Botswana and <a href="/wiki/Southern_Ndebele_people" title="Southern Ndebele people">Ndebele</a> tribes who were making incursions into the territory from the north-east. Tensions also escalated with the Dutch <a href="/wiki/Boer" title="Boer">Boer</a> settlers from the <a href="/wiki/South_African_Republic" title="South African Republic">Transvaal</a> to the east. After appeals by the Batswana leaders <a href="/wiki/Khama_III" title="Khama III">Khama III</a>, Bathoen and Sebele for assistance, the British Government put Bechuanaland under its protection on 31 March 1885.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The northern territory remained under direct administration as the <a href="/wiki/Bechuanaland_Protectorate" title="Bechuanaland Protectorate">Bechuanaland Protectorate</a> and is modern-day Botswana, while the southern territory became part of the <a href="/wiki/British_Cape_Colony" title="British Cape Colony" class="mw-redirect">Cape Colony</a> and is now part of the northwest province of South Africa. The majority of <a href="/wiki/Setswana" title="Setswana" class="mw-redirect">Setswana</a>-speaking people today live in South Africa.</p>
<p>When the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a> was formed in 1910 out of the main British colonies in the region, the Bechuanaland Protectorate, <a href="/wiki/Basutoland" title="Basutoland">Basutoland</a> (now <a href="/wiki/Lesotho" title="Lesotho">Lesotho</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Swaziland" title="Swaziland">Swaziland</a> (the High Commission Territories) were not included, but provision was made for their later incorporation. However, their inhabitants began to be consulted by the UK, and although successive South African governments sought to have the territories transferred, the UK kept delaying; consequently, it never occurred. The election of the <a href="/wiki/National_Party_(South_Africa)" title="National Party (South Africa)">Nationalist</a> government in 1948, which instituted <a href="/wiki/Apartheid" title="Apartheid">apartheid</a>, and South Africa's withdrawal from the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth</a> in 1961, ended any prospect of incorporation of the territories into South Africa. An expansion of British central authority and the evolution of tribal government resulted in the 1920 establishment of two advisory councils to represent both Africans and Europeans. Proclamations in 1934 regulated tribal rule and powers. A European-African advisory council was formed in 1951, and the 1961 constitution established a consultative legislative council.</p>
<p>In June 1964, the UK accepted proposals for a democratic self-government in Botswana. The seat of government was moved in 1965 from <a href="/wiki/Mafeking" title="Mafeking" class="mw-redirect">Mafikeng</a> in South Africa, to the newly established <a href="/wiki/Gaborone" title="Gaborone">Gaborone</a>, which sits near its border. The 1965 constitution led to the first general elections and to independence on 30 September 1966. <a href="/wiki/Seretse_Khama" title="Seretse Khama">Seretse Khama</a>, a leader in the independence movement and the legitimate claimant to the <a href="/wiki/Bamangwato" title="Bamangwato" class="mw-redirect">Ngwato</a> chiefship, was elected as the first President, going on to be re-elected twice.</p>
<p>The presidency passed to the sitting Vice-President, <a href="/wiki/Quett_Masire" title="Quett Masire">Quett Masire</a>, who was elected in his own right in 1984 and re-elected in 1989 and 1994. Masire retired from office in 1998, and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Festus_Mogae" title="Festus Mogae">Festus Mogae</a>, who was elected in his own right in 1999 and re-elected in 2004. The presidency passed in 2008 to <a href="/wiki/Ian_Khama" title="Ian Khama">Ian Khama</a> (son of the first President), who had been serving as Mogae's Vice-President since resigning his position in 1998 as Commander of the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Defence_Force" title="Botswana Defence Force">Botswana Defence Force</a> to take up this civilian role.</p>
<p>A long-running dispute over the northern border with <a href="/wiki/Namibia" title="Namibia">Namibia</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Caprivi_Strip" title="Caprivi Strip">Caprivi Strip</a> was the subject of a ruling by the <a href="/wiki/International_Court_of_Justice" title="International Court of Justice">International Court of Justice</a> in December 1999, which ruled that <a href="/wiki/Kasikili_Island" title="Kasikili Island" class="mw-redirect">Kasikili Island</a> belongs to Botswana.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Botswana" title="Geography of Botswana">Geography of Botswana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Botswana" title="Climate of Botswana" class="mw-redirect">Climate of Botswana</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flying-female-Lechwe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flying-female-Lechwe.jpg/220px-Flying-female-Lechwe.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flying-female-Lechwe.jpg/330px-Flying-female-Lechwe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Flying-female-Lechwe.jpg/440px-Flying-female-Lechwe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3038" data-file-height="2012" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flying-female-Lechwe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Lechwe" title="Lechwe">lechwe</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Okavango_Delta" title="Okavango Delta">Okavango Delta</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At 581,730&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (224,607&#160;sq&#160;mi) Botswana is the world's 48th-largest country. It is comparable in size to <a href="/wiki/Madagascar" title="Madagascar">Madagascar</a> or <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>. It lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/17th_parallel_south" title="17th parallel south">17°</a> and <a href="/wiki/27th_parallel_south" title="27th parallel south">27°S</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/20th_meridian_east" title="20th meridian east">20°</a> and <a href="/wiki/30th_meridian_east" title="30th meridian east">30°E</a>.</p>
<p>The country is predominantly flat, tending toward gently rolling <a href="/wiki/Plateau" title="Plateau">tableland</a>. Botswana is dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari_Desert" title="Kalahari Desert">Kalahari Desert</a>, which covers up to 70% of its land surface. The <a href="/wiki/Okavango_Delta" title="Okavango Delta">Okavango Delta</a>, one of the world's largest inland <a href="/wiki/River_deltas" title="River deltas" class="mw-redirect">deltas</a>, is in the northwest. The <a href="/wiki/Makgadikgadi_Pan" title="Makgadikgadi Pan">Makgadikgadi Pan</a>, a large <a href="/wiki/Salt_pan_(geology)" title="Salt pan (geology)">salt pan</a>, lies in the north.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Limpopo_River" title="Limpopo River">Limpopo River</a> Basin, the major landform of all of southern Africa, lies partly in Botswana, with the basins of its tributaries, the <a href="/wiki/Notwane_River" title="Notwane River">Notwane</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bonwapitse_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bonwapitse River (page does not exist)">Bonwapitse</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mahalapswe_River&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mahalapswe River (page does not exist)">Mahalapswe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lotsane_River" title="Lotsane River">Lotsane</a>, <a href="/wiki/Motloutse_River" title="Motloutse River">Motloutse</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Shashe_River" title="Shashe River">Shashe</a>, located in the eastern part of the country. The Notwane provides water to the capital through the <a href="/wiki/Gaborone_Dam" title="Gaborone Dam">Gaborone Dam</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Cuando_River" title="Cuando River">Chobe River</a> lies to the north, providing a boundary between Botswana and Namibia's <a href="/wiki/Zambezi_Region" title="Zambezi Region">Zambezi Region</a>. The Chobe River meets with the <a href="/wiki/Zambezi" title="Zambezi">Zambezi River</a> at a place called <a href="/wiki/Kazungula" title="Kazungula" class="mw-redirect">Kazungula</a> (meaning a small <a href="/wiki/Sausage_tree" title="Sausage tree" class="mw-redirect">sausage tree</a>, a point where <a href="/wiki/Sebitwane" title="Sebitwane" class="mw-redirect">Sebitwane</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Makololo" title="Makololo" class="mw-redirect">Makololo tribe</a> crossed the Zambezi into Zambia).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Botswana has diverse areas of wildlife habitat. In addition to the delta and desert areas, there are <a href="/wiki/Grassland" title="Grassland">grasslands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Blue_wildebeest" title="Blue wildebeest">blue wildebeest</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antelope" title="Antelope">antelopes</a>, and other mammals and birds are found. Northern Botswana has one of the few remaining large populations of the endangered <a href="/wiki/African_wild_dog" title="African wild dog">African wild dog</a>. <a href="/wiki/Chobe_National_Park" title="Chobe National Park">Chobe National Park</a>, found in the <a href="/wiki/Chobe_District" title="Chobe District">Chobe District</a>, has the world's largest concentration of <a href="/wiki/African_elephant" title="African elephant">African elephants</a>. The park covers about 11,000&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (4,247&#160;sq&#160;mi) and supports about 350 species of birds.</p>
<p>The Chobe National Park and <a href="/wiki/Moremi_Game_Reserve" title="Moremi Game Reserve">Moremi Game Reserve</a> (in the Okavango Delta) are major tourist destinations. Other reserves include the <a href="/wiki/Central_Kalahari_Game_Reserve" title="Central Kalahari Game Reserve">Central Kalahari Game Reserve</a> located in the Kalahari desert in <a href="/wiki/Ghanzi_District" title="Ghanzi District">Ghanzi District</a>; <a href="/wiki/Makgadikgadi_Pans_National_Park" title="Makgadikgadi Pans National Park" class="mw-redirect">Makgadikgadi Pans National Park</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nxai_Pan_National_Park" title="Nxai Pan National Park">Nxai Pan National Park</a> are in <a href="/wiki/Central_District_(Botswana)" title="Central District (Botswana)">Central District</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Makgadikgadi_Pan" title="Makgadikgadi Pan">Makgadikgadi Pan</a>. Mashatu Game Reserve is privately owned: located where the <a href="/wiki/Shashe_River" title="Shashe River">Shashe River</a> and Limpopo River meet in eastern Botswana. The other privately owned reserve is <a href="/wiki/Mokolodi_Nature_Reserve" title="Mokolodi Nature Reserve">Mokolodi Nature Reserve</a> near Gaborone. There are also specialised sanctuaries like the Khama Rhino Sanctuary (for rhinoceros) and Makgadikgadi Sanctuary (for flamingos). They are both located in Central District.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_problems">Environmental problems</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Environmental problems">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Baobob_tree.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Baobob_tree.jpg/170px-Baobob_tree.jpg" width="170" height="254" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Baobob_tree.jpg/255px-Baobob_tree.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Baobob_tree.jpg/340px-Baobob_tree.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1164" data-file-height="1738" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Baobob_tree.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Baobab_tree" title="Baobab tree" class="mw-redirect">baobab tree</a> (<i>Adansonia digitata</i>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Botswana faces two major <a href="/wiki/Natural_environment" title="Natural environment">environmental</a> problems: drought and <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>. The desertification problems predominantly stem from the severe times of drought in the country. Three quarters of the country's human and animal populations depend on groundwater due to drought. <a href="/wiki/Groundwater" title="Groundwater">Groundwater</a> use through deep borehole drilling has somewhat eased the effects of drought. Surface water is scarce in Botswana and less than 5% of the agriculture in the country is sustainable by rainfall. In the remaining 95% of the country, raising livestock is the primary source of rural income. Approximately 71% of the country's land is used for communal <a href="/wiki/Grazing" title="Grazing">grazing</a>, which has been a major cause of the desertification and the accelerating soil erosion of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-rala.is_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rala.is-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Since raising livestock has proven to be profitable for the people of Botswana, the land continues to be exploited. The animal populations have continued to dramatically increase. From 1966 to 1991 the livestock population has increased from 1.7 million to 5.5 million.<sup id="cite_ref-rala.is_12-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rala.is-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:64</sup> Similarly, the human population has increased from 574,000 in 1971 to 1.5 million in 1995, nearly a 200% increase. "Over 50% of all households in Botswana own cattle, which is currently the largest single source of rural income." "Rangeland degradation or desertification is regarded as the reduction in land productivity as a result of overstocking and overgrazing or as a result of veld product gathering for commercial use. Degradation is exacerbated by the effects of drought and climate change."<sup id="cite_ref-rala.is_12-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rala.is-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> Environmentalists report that the <a href="/wiki/Okavango_Delta" title="Okavango Delta">Okavango Delta</a> is drying up due to the increased grazing of livestock.<sup id="cite_ref-afrol.com_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afrol.com-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> The Okavango Delta is one of the major semi-forested wetlands in Botswana and one of the largest inland deltas in the world; it is a crucial ecosystem to the survival of many animals.<sup id="cite_ref-afrol.com_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afrol.com-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Department of Forestry and Range Resources has already begun to implement a project to reintroduce indigenous vegetation into communities in Kgalagadi South, Kweneng North and Boteti.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Reintroduction of indigenous vegetation will help with the degradation of the land. The <a href="/wiki/United_States_Government" title="United States Government" class="mw-redirect">United States Government</a> has also entered into an agreement with Botswana, giving them $7 million US dollars to reduce Botswana's debt by $8.3 million US dollars. The stipulation of the US reducing Botswana's debt is that Botswana will focus on more extensive <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">conservation</a> of the land.<sup id="cite_ref-afrol.com_13-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afrol.com-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Development_Programme" title="United Nations Development Programme">United Nations Development Programme</a> claims that poverty is a major problem behind the overexploitation of resources, including land, in Botswana. To help change this the UNDP joined in with a project started in the southern community of Struizendam in Botswana. The purpose of the project is to draw from "indigenous knowledge and traditional land management systems". The leaders of this movement are supposed to be the people in the community, to draw them in, in turn increasing their possibilities to earn an income and thus decreasing poverty. The UNDP also stated that the government has to effectively implement policies to allow people to manage their own local resources and are giving the government information to help with policy development<sup id="cite_ref-afrol1_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afrol1-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics_and_government">Politics and government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Politics and government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BotswanaParliament.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/BotswanaParliament.jpg/220px-BotswanaParliament.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/BotswanaParliament.jpg/330px-BotswanaParliament.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d0/BotswanaParliament.jpg/440px-BotswanaParliament.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BotswanaParliament.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
House of the Parliament of Botswana in <a href="/wiki/Gaborone" title="Gaborone">Gaborone</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Botswana" title="Politics of Botswana">Politics of Botswana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Botswana" title="Human rights in Botswana">Human rights in Botswana</a></div>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Botswana" title="Foreign relations of Botswana">Foreign relations of Botswana</a></div>
<p>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.botswanaembassy.org/files/constitution_of_botswana.pdf">Constitution of Botswana</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Rule_of_law" title="Rule of law">rule of law</a> which protects the citizens of Botswana and represents their rights. The politics of Botswana take place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democratic</a> republic, whereby the <a href="/wiki/President_of_Botswana" title="President of Botswana" class="mw-redirect">President of Botswana</a> is both <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>, and of a <a href="/wiki/Multi-party_system" title="Multi-party system">multi-party system</a>. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power" class="mw-redirect">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power" class="mw-redirect">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Botswana" title="Parliament of Botswana">Parliament of Botswana</a>. <a href="/wiki/Botswana_general_election,_2014" title="Botswana general election, 2014">The most recent election</a>, its eleventh, was held on 24 October 2014.</p>
<p>Since independence was declared, the party system has been dominated by the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Democratic_Party" title="Botswana Democratic Party">Botswana Democratic Party</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judiciary</a> is independent of the executive and the legislature. Botswana ranks 30th out of 167 states in the 2012 <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">Democracy Index</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-index2012_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-index2012-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International</a>, Botswana is the least corrupt country in Africa and ranks close to Portugal and South Korea.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations_and_military">Foreign relations and military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Foreign relations and military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Defence_Force" title="Botswana Defence Force">Botswana Defence Force</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Welcome_to_Botswana,_signs.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Welcome_to_Botswana%2C_signs.jpg/220px-Welcome_to_Botswana%2C_signs.jpg" width="220" height="87" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Welcome_to_Botswana%2C_signs.jpg/330px-Welcome_to_Botswana%2C_signs.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Welcome_to_Botswana%2C_signs.jpg/440px-Welcome_to_Botswana%2C_signs.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1912" data-file-height="756" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Welcome_to_Botswana,_signs.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Signs at the Botswana-<a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a> border, 2010</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>At the time of independence, Botswana had no armed forces. It was only after the <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">Rhodesian</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_African_Army" title="South African Army">South African</a> militaries struck respectively against the <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe_People%27s_Revolutionary_Army" title="Zimbabwe People's Revolutionary Army">Zimbabwe People's Revolutionary Army</a> and <a href="/wiki/Umkhonto_we_Sizwe" title="Umkhonto we Sizwe">Umkhonto we Sizwe</a><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> bases that the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Defence_Force" title="Botswana Defence Force">Botswana Defence Force</a> (BDF) was formed in 1977.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The President is <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a> of the armed forces and appoints a defence council. The BDF has approximately 12,000 members.</p>
<p>Following political changes in South Africa and the region, the BDF's missions have increasingly focused on prevention of <a href="/wiki/Poaching" title="Poaching">poaching</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emergency_management" title="Emergency management">preparing for disasters</a>, and foreign <a href="/wiki/Peacekeeping" title="Peacekeeping">peacekeeping</a>. The United States has been the largest single foreign contributor to the development of the BDF, and a large segment of its officer corps have received U.S. training. It is considered an apolitical and professional institution.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The Botswana government gave the United States the green light to explore the possibility of establishing an Africa Command (Africom) base in the country.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Botswana" title="Districts of Botswana">Districts of Botswana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sub-districts_of_Botswana" title="Sub-districts of Botswana">Sub-districts of Botswana</a></div>
<p>Botswana is divided into nine districts.</p>

<p>Botswana is further divided into 15 councils which includes the 9 districts councils from the 9 districts plus some councils from urban or town councils being:</p>
<ol>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gaborone" title="Gaborone">Gaborone</a> City</li>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Debswana_HQ.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Debswana_HQ.jpg/220px-Debswana_HQ.jpg" width="220" height="122" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Debswana_HQ.jpg/330px-Debswana_HQ.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/14/Debswana_HQ.jpg/440px-Debswana_HQ.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3644" data-file-height="2017" /></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Botswana" title="Economy of Botswana">Economy of Botswana</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Botswana" title="Bank of Botswana">Bank of Botswana</a> serves as a <a href="/wiki/Central_bank" title="Central bank">central bank</a> in order to develop and maintain the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_pula" title="Botswana pula">Botswana pula</a>, the country's currency. Since independence, Botswana has had one of the fastest growth rates in per capita income in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Botswana has transformed itself from one of the poorest countries in the world to a middle-income country. By one estimate, it has the fourth highest <a href="/wiki/Gross_national_income" title="Gross national income">gross national income</a> at <a href="/wiki/Purchasing_power_parity" title="Purchasing power parity">purchasing power parity</a> in Africa, giving it a standard of living around that of Mexico and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mti.gov.bw/">Ministry of Trade and Industry of Botswana</a> is responsible for promoting <a href="/wiki/Business_development" title="Business development">business development</a> throughout the country. According to the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a>, economic growth averaged over 9% per year from 1966 to 1999. Botswana has a <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_economic_freedom" title="List of countries by economic freedom">high level of economic freedom</a> compared to other African countries.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> The government has maintained a sound <a href="/wiki/Fiscal_policy" title="Fiscal policy">fiscal policy</a>, despite consecutive <a href="/wiki/Government_budget_deficit" title="Government budget deficit" class="mw-redirect">budget deficits</a> in 2002 and 2003, and a negligible level of <a href="/wiki/External_debt" title="External debt">foreign debt</a>. It earned the highest sovereign <a href="/wiki/Credit_rating" title="Credit rating">credit rating</a> in Africa and has stockpiled foreign exchange reserves (over $7 billion in 2005/2006) amounting to almost two and a half years of current imports.</p>
<p>An array of financial institutions populates the country's financial system, with pension funds and commercial banks being the two most important segments by asset size. Banks remain profitable, well-capitalised, and liquid, as a result of growing national resources and high interest rates.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Botswana's competitive banking system is one of Africa's most advanced.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (September 2010)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Generally adhering to global standards in the transparency of financial policies and banking supervision, the financial sector provides ample access to credit for entrepreneurs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The opening of Capital Bank in 2008 brought the total number of licensed banks to eight.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The government is involved in banking through state-owned financial institutions and a special financial incentives program that is aimed at increasing Botswana's status as a financial centre.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Credit is allocated on market terms, although the government provides subsidised loans.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Reform of <a href="/wiki/Non-bank_financial_institution" title="Non-bank financial institution">non-bank financial institutions</a> has continued in recent years, notably through the establishment of a single financial regulatory agency that provides more effective supervision.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The government has abolished exchange controls, and with the resulting creation of new portfolio investment options, the Botswana Stock Exchange is growing.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Botswana_trade.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Botswana_trade.png/220px-Botswana_trade.png" width="220" height="97" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Botswana_trade.png/330px-Botswana_trade.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/61/Botswana_trade.png/440px-Botswana_trade.png 2x" data-file-width="1083" data-file-height="479" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Botswana_trade.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Botswana's trading partners in 2004</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The constitution prohibits the nationalisation of private property and provides for an independent judiciary, and the government respects this in practice. The legal system is sufficient to conduct secure commercial dealings, although a serious and growing backlog of cases prevents timely trials. The protection of intellectual property rights has improved significantly. Botswana is ranked second only to South Africa among sub-Saharan Africa countries in the 2009 International Property Rights Index.</p>
<p>While generally open to foreign participation in its economy, Botswana reserves some sectors for citizens. Increased foreign investment plays a significant role in the privatisation of state-owned enterprises. Investment regulations are transparent, and bureaucratic procedures are streamlined and open, although somewhat slow. Investment returns such as profits and dividends, debt service, capital gains, returns on intellectual property, royalties, franchise's fees, and service fees can be repatriated without limits.</p>
<p>Botswana imports refined petroleum products and electricity from South Africa. There is some domestic production of electricity from coal. In spite of one of the highest insolation levels in the world, Botswana has no significant solar energy capacity.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gemstones_and_precious_metals">Gemstones and precious metals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Gemstones and precious metals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In Botswana, the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.mines.gov.bw/">Department of Mines</a> and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.gov.bw/">Ministry of Minerals, Energy and Water Resources</a>, led by Hon Onkokame Kitso Mokaila in Gaborone, maintains data regarding mining throughout the country. <a href="/wiki/Debswana" title="Debswana">Debswana</a>, the largest <a href="/wiki/List_of_diamond_mines" title="List of diamond mines">diamond mining</a> company operating in Botswana, is 50% owned by the government.<sup id="cite_ref-botswana_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-botswana-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The mineral industry provides about 40% of all government revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-worldbankbotswana_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldbankbotswana-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, significant quantities of uranium were discovered, and mining was projected to begin by 2010. Several international mining corporations have established regional headquarters in Botswana, and prospected for diamonds, gold, uranium, copper, and even oil, many coming back with positive results. Government announced in early 2009 that they would try to shift their economic dependence on diamonds, over serious concern that diamonds are predicted to dry out in Botswana over the next twenty years.</p>
<p>Botswana’s Orapa mine is the largest diamond mine in the world in terms of value and quantity of carats produced annually.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Estimated to produce over 11 million carats in 2013, with an average price of $145/carat, the Orapa mine is estimated to produce over $1.6 billion worth of diamonds in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-Kitco_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kitco-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Botswana" title="Demographics of Botswana">Demographics of Botswana</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gathering_food_in_the_Okavango.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Gathering_food_in_the_Okavango.jpg/220px-Gathering_food_in_the_Okavango.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Gathering_food_in_the_Okavango.jpg/330px-Gathering_food_in_the_Okavango.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Gathering_food_in_the_Okavango.jpg/440px-Gathering_food_in_the_Okavango.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gathering_food_in_the_Okavango.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A girl in the <a href="/wiki/Okavango_Delta" title="Okavango Delta">Okavango Delta</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tswana_people" title="Tswana people">Tswana</a> are the majority ethnic group in Botswana, making up 79% of the population. The largest minority ethnic groups are the <a href="/wiki/BaKalanga" title="BaKalanga" class="mw-redirect">BaKalanga</a>, <a href="/wiki/San_people" title="San people">San</a> or <a href="/w/index.php?title=AbaThwa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="AbaThwa (page does not exist)">AbaThwa</a> also known as Basarwa. Other tribes are <a href="/wiki/Bayei" title="Bayei" class="mw-redirect">Bayei</a>, Bambukushu, <a href="/wiki/Basubia" title="Basubia" class="mw-redirect">Basubia</a>, Baherero and Bakgalagadi. In addition, there are small numbers of whites and Indians, both groups being roughly equally small in number. <a href="/wiki/Indians_in_Botswana" title="Indians in Botswana">Botswana's Indian</a> population is made up of many Indian-Africans of several generations, from Mozambique, Kenya, Tanzania, Mauritius, South Africa, and so on, as well as first generation Indian immigrants. The white population speaks English and <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans" title="Afrikaans">Afrikaans</a> and makes up roughly 3% of the population.</p>
<p>Since 2000, because of deteriorating economic conditions in Zimbabwe, the number of <a href="/wiki/Zimbabweans_in_Botswana" title="Zimbabweans in Botswana">Zimbabweans in Botswana</a> has risen into the tens of thousands.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Fewer than 10,000 San are still living the traditional <a href="/wiki/Hunter-gatherer" title="Hunter-gatherer">hunter-gatherer</a> style of life. Since the mid-1990s the central government of Botswana has been trying to move San out of their lands.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The UN's top official on <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_rights" title="Indigenous rights">indigenous rights</a>, Prof. <a href="/wiki/James_Anaya" title="James Anaya">James Anaya</a>, condemned Botswana's actions toward the San in a report released in February 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Botswana" title="Languages of Botswana">Languages of Botswana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Setswana" title="Setswana" class="mw-redirect">Setswana</a></div>
<p>The official language of Botswana is English although <a href="/wiki/Tswana_language" title="Tswana language">Setswana</a> is widely spoken across the country. In Setswana, <a href="/wiki/Prefix" title="Prefix">prefixes</a> are more important than they are in many other languages. These prefixes include <i>Bo</i>, which refers to the country, <i>Ba</i>, which refers to the people, <i>Mo</i>, which is one person, and <i>Se</i> which is the language. For example, the main tribe of Botswana is the Tswana people, hence the name Botswana for its country. The people as a whole are Batswana, one person is a Motswana, and the language they speak is Setswana. Other languages spoken in Botswana include <a href="/wiki/Kalanga_language" title="Kalanga language">Kalanga</a> (sekalanga), <a href="/wiki/Tshwa_language" title="Tshwa language">Sarwa</a> (sesarwa), <a href="/wiki/Northern_Ndebele_language" title="Northern Ndebele language">Ndebele</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taa_language" title="Taa language">!Xóõ</a> and in some parts <a href="/wiki/Afrikaans_language" title="Afrikaans language" class="mw-redirect">Afrikaans</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Botswana" title="Religion in Botswana">Religion in Botswana</a></div>
<div class="barbox tright" style="border:1px solid silver; font-size:88%; padding:0.4em; width:auto; background: white;">
