<p>An estimated 70% of the country's citizens identify themselves as Christians. Anglicans, Methodists, and the United Congregational Church of Southern Africa make up the majority of Christians. There are also congregations of Lutherans, Baptists, the Dutch Reformed Church, Mennonites, Roman Catholics, Seventh-day Adventists, Mormons and Jehovah's Witnesses in the country. In Gaborone, there is a Lutheran History Centre which is open to the public.</p>
<p>According to the 2001 census, the country has around 5,000 Muslims, mainly from South Asia, 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Hindus" title="Hindus" class="mw-redirect">Hindus</a> and 700 <a href="/wiki/Baha%27is" title="Baha'is" class="mw-redirect">Baha'is</a>. Approximately 20% of citizens espouse no religion. Religious services are well attended in both rural and urban areas.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Southern_Accord_2012_Forces_Experience_Cultural_Day_in_Botswana_(7745454444).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Southern_Accord_2012_Forces_Experience_Cultural_Day_in_Botswana_%287745454444%29.jpg/170px-Southern_Accord_2012_Forces_Experience_Cultural_Day_in_Botswana_%287745454444%29.jpg" width="170" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Southern_Accord_2012_Forces_Experience_Cultural_Day_in_Botswana_%287745454444%29.jpg/255px-Southern_Accord_2012_Forces_Experience_Cultural_Day_in_Botswana_%287745454444%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Southern_Accord_2012_Forces_Experience_Cultural_Day_in_Botswana_%287745454444%29.jpg/340px-Southern_Accord_2012_Forces_Experience_Cultural_Day_in_Botswana_%287745454444%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1620" data-file-height="2250" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Southern_Accord_2012_Forces_Experience_Cultural_Day_in_Botswana_(7745454444).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Dance at a cultural day</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Botswana" title="Culture of Botswana">Culture of Botswana</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Khutse_Kalahari_Lodge.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Khutse_Kalahari_Lodge.jpg/220px-Khutse_Kalahari_Lodge.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Khutse_Kalahari_Lodge.jpg/330px-Khutse_Kalahari_Lodge.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Khutse_Kalahari_Lodge.jpg/440px-Khutse_Kalahari_Lodge.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Khutse_Kalahari_Lodge.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A <a href="/wiki/Rondavel" title="Rondavel">rondavel</a> at a lodge near the Kalahari Desert.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Besides referring to the language of the dominant people groups in Botswana, Setswana is the adjective used to describe the rich cultural traditions of the Batswana—whether construed as members of the Tswana ethnic groups or of all citizens of Botswana.</p>
<p>The Scottish writer <a href="/wiki/Alexander_McCall_Smith" title="Alexander McCall Smith">Alexander McCall Smith</a> has written popular novels (<a href="/wiki/No._1_Ladies%27_Detective_Agency" title="No. 1 Ladies' Detective Agency" class="mw-redirect">No. 1 Ladies' Detective Agency</a> series) about Botswana that entertain as well as inform the reader about the culture and customs of Botswana.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Botswana" title="Music of Botswana">Music of Botswana</a></div>
<p>Botswana music is mostly vocal and performed sometimes without drums depending on the occasion; it also makes heavy use of string instruments. Botswana folk music has instruments such as Setinkane (a Botswana version of miniature piano), Segankure/Segaba (a Botswana version of the Chinese instrument Erhu), Moropa (Meropa -plural) (a Botswana version of the many varieties of drums), phala (a Botswana version of a whistle used mostly during celebrations. It comes in variety of forms too). Botswana cultural musical instruments are not confined only to the strings or drums. the hands are used as musical instruments too, by either clapping them together or against phathisi (goat skin turned inside out wrapped around the calf area; it is only used by men) to create music and rhythm. For the last few decades, the guitar has been celebrated as a versatile music instrument for Tswana music as it offers a variety in string which the Segaba instrument does not have. It is the outsider that found a home within the culture. The highlight of any celebration or event that shows especially happiness is the dancing. This differs by regime, age, gender and status in the group or if it's a tribal activity, your status in the community. The national anthem is <a href="/wiki/Fatshe_leno_la_rona" title="Fatshe leno la rona">Fatshe leno la rona</a>. Written and composed by Kgalemang Tumediso Motsete, it was adopted upon independence in 1966.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_arts">Visual arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Visual arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:San_apron-Botswana.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/San_apron-Botswana.jpg/220px-San_apron-Botswana.jpg" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/San_apron-Botswana.jpg/330px-San_apron-Botswana.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/San_apron-Botswana.jpg/440px-San_apron-Botswana.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2839" data-file-height="1936" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:San_apron-Botswana.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Textile art</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Art_of_Botswana" title="Art of Botswana" class="mw-redirect">Art of Botswana</a></div>
<p>In the northern part of Botswana, women in the villages of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Etsha&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Etsha (page does not exist)">Etsha</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gumare" title="Gumare">Gumare</a> are noted for their skill at crafting baskets from Botswana from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mokola_Palm&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mokola Palm (page does not exist)">Mokola Palm</a> and local <a href="/wiki/Dye" title="Dye">dyes</a>. The baskets are generally woven into three types: large, lidded baskets used for storage, large, open baskets for carrying objects on the head or for winnowing threshed grain, and smaller plates for winnowing pounded grain. The artistry of these baskets is being steadily enhanced through colour use and improved designs as they are increasingly produced for commercial use.</p>
<p>Other notable artistic communities include <a href="/w/index.php?title=Thamaga_Pottery&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Thamaga Pottery (page does not exist)">Thamaga Pottery</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Oodi_Weavers&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Oodi Weavers (page does not exist)">Oodi Weavers</a>, both located in the south-eastern part of Botswana.</p>
<p>The oldest paintings from both Botswana and South Africa depict hunting, animal and human figures, and were made by the Khoisan (!Kung San/Bushmen) over twenty thousand years ago within the <a href="/wiki/Kalahari" title="Kalahari" class="mw-redirect">Kalahari</a> desert.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Food">Food</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Food">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boerewors_raw.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Boerewors_raw.jpg/220px-Boerewors_raw.jpg" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Boerewors_raw.jpg/330px-Boerewors_raw.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Boerewors_raw.jpg/440px-Boerewors_raw.jpg 2x" data-file-width="466" data-file-height="354" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boerewors_raw.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Boerewors" title="Boerewors">Boerewors</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Cuisine_of_Botswana" title="Cuisine of Botswana" class="mw-redirect">Cuisine of Botswana</a></div>
<p>The cuisine of Botswana is unique but also shares some characteristics with other cuisine of Southern Africa. Examples of Botswana food are <a href="/wiki/Pap_(food)" title="Pap (food)">pap</a>, <a href="/wiki/Boerewors" title="Boerewors">boerewors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samp" title="Samp">samp</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vetkoek" title="Vetkoek">vetkoek</a> and <a href="/wiki/Imbrasia_belina" title="Imbrasia belina" class="mw-redirect">mopani worms</a>. A food unique to Botswana includes <a href="/wiki/Seswaa" title="Seswaa">seswaa</a>, heavily <a href="/wiki/Salted_meat" title="Salted meat" class="mw-redirect">salted</a> mashed-up meat.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Botswana_at_the_Olympics" title="Botswana at the Olympics">Botswana at the Olympics</a></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">Football</a> is the most popular sport in Botswana, with qualification for the <a href="/wiki/2012_Africa_Cup_of_Nations" title="2012 Africa Cup of Nations">2012 Africa Cup of Nations</a> being the biggest achievement to date. Other popular sports are <a href="/wiki/Cricket" title="Cricket">cricket</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">tennis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rugby_football" title="Rugby football">rugby</a>, badminton, softball, <a href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball" class="mw-redirect">handball</a>, golf, and track and field.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> Botswana is an associate member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Cricket_Council" title="International Cricket Council">International Cricket Council</a>. Botswana became a member of The International Badminton Federation and Africa Badminton Federation in 1991. Presently, the Botswana Golf Union offers an <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.botswanagolfunion.org.bw/page2.html">amateur golf league</a> in which golfers compete in tournaments and championships.</p>
<p>Botswana won its first Olympic medal in 2012 when <a href="/wiki/Nijel_Amos" title="Nijel Amos">Nijel Amos</a> won silver in the <a href="/wiki/Athletics_at_the_2012_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_800_metres" title="Athletics at the 2012 Summer Olympics – Men's 800 metres">800 metres</a>. In 2011 <a href="/wiki/Amantle_Montsho" title="Amantle Montsho">Amantle Montsho</a> became <a href="/wiki/2011_World_Championships_in_Athletics_%E2%80%93_Women%27s_400_metres" title="2011 World Championships in Athletics – Women's 400 metres">world champion</a> in the 400 metres and won Botswana's first athletics medal on the world level. Another famous Botswana athlete is high jumper <a href="/wiki/Kabelo_Kgosiemang" title="Kabelo Kgosiemang">Kabelo Kgosiemang</a>, three times <a href="/wiki/African_Championships_in_Athletics" title="African Championships in Athletics">African champion</a>.</p>
<p>The card game <a href="/wiki/Contract_bridge" title="Contract bridge">bridge</a> has a strong following; it was first played in Botswana over 30 years ago and grew in popularity during the 1980s. Many British expatriate school teachers informally taught the game in Botswana's secondary schools. The Botswana Bridge Federation (BBF) was founded in 1988 and continues to organise tournaments. Bridge has remained popular and the BBF has over 800 members.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, the BBF invited the <a href="/wiki/English_Bridge_Union" title="English Bridge Union">English Bridge Union</a> to host a week-long teaching program in May 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:GABS-UB_Courtyard.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/GABS-UB_Courtyard.JPG/220px-GABS-UB_Courtyard.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/GABS-UB_Courtyard.JPG/330px-GABS-UB_Courtyard.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/GABS-UB_Courtyard.JPG/440px-GABS-UB_Courtyard.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:GABS-UB_Courtyard.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Buildings of the new and old Botswana university. Botswana's economic growth has had a positive impact on the university.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Botswana" title="Education in Botswana">Education in Botswana</a></div>
<p>Botswana has made great strides in educational development since independence in 1966. At that time there were very few graduates in the country and only a very small percentage of the population attended secondary school. Botswana increased its adult literacy rate from 69% in 1991 to 83% in 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-ref_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>With the discovery of diamonds and the increase in government revenue that this brought, there was a huge increase in educational provision in the country. All students were guaranteed ten years of basic education, leading to a Junior Certificate qualification. Approximately half of the school population attends a further two years of secondary schooling leading to the award of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana_General_Certificate_of_Secondary_Education&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Botswana General Certificate of Secondary Education (page does not exist)">Botswana General Certificate of Secondary Education</a> (BGCSE). Secondary education in Botswana is neither free nor compulsory.</p>
<p>After leaving school, students can attend one of the seven technical colleges in the country, or take vocational training courses in <a href="/wiki/Teaching" title="Teaching" class="mw-redirect">teaching</a> or <a href="/wiki/Nursing" title="Nursing">nursing</a>. The best students enter the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Botswana" title="University of Botswana">University of Botswana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Botswana_College_of_Agriculture" title="Botswana College of Agriculture">Botswana College of Agriculture</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Accountancy_College" title="Botswana Accountancy College">Botswana Accountancy College</a> in Gaborone. Many other students end up in the numerous private tertiary education colleges around the country. Notable amongst these is <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.bothocollege.ac.bw/">Botho University</a>, the country's first private university which offers undergraduate programmes in Accounting, Business and Computing. Another international university is the <a href="/wiki/Limkokwing_University_of_Creative_Technology" title="Limkokwing University of Creative Technology">Limkokwing University of Creative Technology</a> which offers various Associate Degrees in Creative Arts.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Other tertiary institutions include <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.baisago.co.bw/">Ba Isago</a>, ABM University College, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.neweracollege.ac.bw/">New Era</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.gips.ac.bw/gips.php">Gaborone Institute of Professional Studies</a> etc. Tremendous strides in providing quality education have been made by private education providers such that a large number of the best students in the country are now applying to them as well.A vast majority of these students are government sponsored. A larger influx of tertiary students is expected when construction of the nation's second international university, The <a href="/wiki/Botswana_International_University_of_Science_and_Technology" title="Botswana International University of Science and Technology">Botswana International University of Science and Technology</a>, is completed in <a href="/wiki/Palapye" title="Palapye">Palapye</a>.</p>
<p>The quantitative gains have not always been matched by qualitative ones. Primary schools in particular still lack resources, and the teachers are less well paid than their secondary school colleagues. The <a href="/wiki/Botswana_Ministry_of_Education" title="Botswana Ministry of Education" class="mw-redirect">Botswana Ministry of Education</a><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> is working to establish libraries in primary schools in partnership with the <a href="/wiki/African_Library_Project" title="African Library Project">African Library Project</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Botswana" title="Government of Botswana" class="mw-redirect">Government of Botswana</a> hopes that by investing a large part of national income in education, the country will become less dependent on diamonds for its economic survival, and less dependent on expatriates for its skilled workers.<sup id="cite_ref-UNEVOC_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNEVOC-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Those objectives are in part pursued through policies in favour of vocational education, gathered within the NPVET (National Policy on Vocational Education and Training, aiming to "integrate the different types of vocational education and training into one comprehensive system".<sup id="cite_ref-UNEVOC_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UNEVOC-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> Botswana invests 21% of its government spending in education.<sup id="cite_ref-ref_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ref-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In January 2006, Botswana announced the reintroduction of school fees after two decades of free state education<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> though the government still provides full scholarships with living expenses to any Botswana citizen in university, either at the University of Botswana or if the student wishes to pursue an education in any field not offered locally, such as medicine, they are provided with a full scholarship to study abroad.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_Botswana" title="Health in Botswana">Health in Botswana</a></div>
<p>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.moh.gov.bw/">Ministry of Health</a> in Botswana is responsible for overseeing the quality and distribution of <a href="/wiki/Healthcare" title="Healthcare" class="mw-redirect">healthcare</a> throughout the country. <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">Life expectancy</a> at birth was 55 in 2009 according to the World Bank, having previously fallen from a peak of 64.1 in 1990 to a low of 49 in 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cancer_Association_of_Botswana" title="Cancer Association of Botswana">Cancer Association of Botswana</a> is a voluntary non-governmental organisation. The association is a member of the Union for International Cancer Control. The Association supplements existing services through provision of cancer prevention and health awareness programmes, facilitating access to health services for cancer patients and offering support and counseling to those affected.<sup id="cite_ref-UICC_Cancer_Association_of_Botswana_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UICC_Cancer_Association_of_Botswana-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="HIV.2FAIDS_epidemic">HIV/AIDS epidemic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: HIV/AIDS epidemic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Botswana" title="HIV/AIDS in Botswana">HIV/AIDS in Botswana</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries,_1960_to_2002.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries%2C_1960_to_2002.svg/220px-Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries%2C_1960_to_2002.svg.png" width="220" height="155" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries%2C_1960_to_2002.svg/330px-Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries%2C_1960_to_2002.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/36/Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries%2C_1960_to_2002.svg/440px-Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries%2C_1960_to_2002.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1459" data-file-height="1027" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Life_expectancy_in_select_Southern_African_countries,_1960_to_2002.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Life expectancy in several African countries from 1960 to 2002. Botswana had the highest life expectancy until <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS" title="HIV/AIDS">HIV/AIDS</a> began to reduce it in the late 1980s.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Like elsewhere in Sub-Saharan Africa, the <a href="/wiki/Economic_impact_of_AIDS" title="Economic impact of AIDS" class="mw-redirect">economic impact of AIDS</a> is considerable. Economic development spending was cut by 10% in 2002–3 as a result of recurring budget deficits and rising expenditure on healthcare services. <a href="/wiki/HIV/AIDS_in_Botswana" title="HIV/AIDS in Botswana">Botswana has been hit</a> very hard by the <a href="/wiki/AIDS_pandemic" title="AIDS pandemic" class="mw-redirect">AIDS pandemic</a>; in 2006 it was estimated that life expectancy at birth had dropped from 65 to 35 years.<sup id="cite_ref-Kallings_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kallings-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> However, after Botswana's 2011 census current life expectancy is estimated at 54.06 years.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> This revision shows the difficulty of accurately estimating the prevalence and impact of HIV/AIDS in the absence of hard numbers.</p>
<p>The prevalence of HIV/AIDS in Botswana was estimated at 24% for adults in 2006,<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> giving Botswana the second highest infection rate in the world after nearby <a href="/wiki/Swaziland" title="Swaziland">Swaziland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2003, the government began a comprehensive program involving free or cheap generic <a href="/wiki/Antiretroviral_drug" title="Antiretroviral drug" class="mw-redirect">anti-retroviral</a> drugs as well as an information campaign designed to stop the spread of the virus. A nation-wide Prevention of Mother-to-Child Transmission program. Botswana has reduced HIV transmission from infected mothers to their children from about 40% to just 4%. Under the leadership of <a href="/wiki/Festus_Mogae" title="Festus Mogae">Festus Mogae</a>, the Government of Botswana solicited outside help in fighting HIV/AIDS and received early support from the <a href="/wiki/Bill_and_Melinda_Gates_Foundation" title="Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation" class="mw-redirect">Bill and Melinda Gates Foundation</a>, the Merck Foundation, and together formed the African Comprehensive HIV AIDS Partnership (ACHAP). Other early partners include the <a href="/wiki/Botswana-Harvard_AIDS_Institute" title="Botswana-Harvard AIDS Institute" class="mw-redirect">Botswana-Harvard AIDS Institute</a>, of the <a href="/wiki/Harvard_School_of_Public_Health" title="Harvard School of Public Health" class="mw-redirect">Harvard School of Public Health</a> and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana-UPenn_Partnership&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Botswana-UPenn Partnership (page does not exist)">Botswana-UPenn Partnership</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Pennsylvania" title="University of Pennsylvania">University of Pennsylvania</a>. According to the 2011 UNAIDS Report, universal access to treatment – defined as 80% coverage or greater – has been achieved in Botswana.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Potential reasons for Botswana's high HIV prevalence include concurrent sexual partnerships, transactional sex, cross-generational sex, and a significant number of people who travel outside of their local communities in pursuit of work. The <a href="/wiki/Polyamory" title="Polyamory">polyamorous</a> nature of many sexual relationships further impacts the health situation, to the extent that it has given rise to a Love Vocabulary<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> that is unique to the region.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Botswana&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.botswanatourism.co.bw/">Botswana Tourism Organisation</a> is the country's official tourism group. Primarily, tourists visit Gaborone due to the city having numerous activities for visitors. Hotels include; The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.lonrhohotels.com/content/lansmore-masa-square">Lonrho Lansmore Masa Square</a>, a 5-Star hotel, and The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.suninternational.com/gaborone-sun/Pages/default.aspx">Gaborone Sun</a>, a luxury hotel that also features a <a href="/wiki/Casino" title="Casino">casino</a>. The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.lionpark.co.bw/">Lion Park Resort</a> is Botswana's first permanent <a href="/wiki/Amusement_park" title="Amusement park">amusement park</a> and hosts events such as <a href="/wiki/Birthday_party#Birthday_party" title="Birthday party" class="mw-redirect">birthday parties</a> for families. In Botswana, there are also destinations which include; The Gaborone Yacht Club and The Kalahari Fishing Club. In addition, natural attractions for tourists in Botswana include; The Gaborone Dam and Mokolodi Nature Reserve. There are <a href="/wiki/Golf_course" title="Golf course">golf courses</a> which are maintained by the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.botswanagolfunion.org.bw/">Botswana Golf Union (BGU)</a>. The Phakalane Golf Estate is a multi-million dollar clubhouse that offers both hotel accommodations and access to golf courses.</p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Museums" title="Museums" class="mw-redirect">Museums</a> in Botswana include;</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Botswana_National_Museum" title="Botswana National Museum">Botswana National Museum</a> in Gaborone</li>
<li>Kgosi Bathoen II (Segopotso) Museum in Kanye</li>
<li>Kgosi Sechele I Museum in Molepolole</li>
<li>Khama III Memorial Museum in Serowe</li>
<li>Nhabe Museum in Maun</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Phuthadikobo_Museum" title="Phuthadikobo Museum">Phuthadikobo Museum</a> in Mochudi</li>
<li>Supa Ngwano Museum Centre in Francistown</li>
</ul>
